item_0.note: The case Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-1031] for client Christopher Wilkerson has completed comprehensive file organization using an eight-bucket structure. Phase 1, Inventory, is complete: a total file inventory of 197 files was generated, .md filenames were scrambled to eliminate naming bias, and a PDF-to-MD mapping was created to aid reunification.

Phase 2, Analysis & Mapping, is complete as well. Eleven parallel sub-agents were deployed to process the 197 files (approximately 40 per agent), and work proceeded in three batches: 4, 4, and 3 sub-agents. A comprehensive reorganization map was created for 170 files, with the proper naming convention applied: YYYY-MM-DD - Client Name - Category - Originator - Description. Additionally, 11 duplicate files were identified for deletion.

Phase 3, Quality Review, is finished with an error rate of 2.35% (4 errors out of 170 files). The main agent corrected those 4 errors: 3 category errors were fixed (Litigation revised to Insurance/Client/Case Information), 1 date error was corrected (injury date changed to form completion date), and a multi-case document was approved for split (a PIP worksheet that included unrelated lien letters).

Phase 4, Execution, is complete as well. There were 164 file operations, and 217 files were moved into the proper eight-bucket structure. The distribution was as follows: Case Information: 2 files (PPD Calculator); Client: 57 files (intake forms, WC forms, health insurance cards); Investigation: 13 files (police report, accident photos, driver license); Medical Records: 64 files (treatment notes, MMI reports, HIPAA authorizations); Insurance: 76 files (WC/PIP correspondence, policy documents); Expenses: 1 file (LexisNexis receipt); Negotiation Settlement: 2 files (settlement demand); Litigation: 2 files (employment history form). Eleven duplicate files were deleted, and PDFs were reunified with their .md companions.

Phase 5, Verification, is complete. All eight bucket directories were created successfully, and all moved files follow the proper naming convention with no loose files remaining in the root directory. Minor cleanup remains: 49 EML files require .md companions, and 4 orphaned hash files require review.

Case context: this is a Workers’ Compensation plus motor vehicle accident case involving a dump truck rollover on [DOB-2]. The client reached maximum medical improvement on [DOB-3] with a 5–8% functional impairment rating. The workers’ compensation carrier is Hartford Mutual (Clearpath), Claim #238042. The PIP carrier is Kentucky Farm Bureau, Claim #04943051.

Result: the case file is now organized with the proper eight-bucket structure and a standardized naming convention. Files are properly categorized and easily retrievable. Quality metrics show 97.65% accuracy in categorization and 100% accuracy in duplicate detection.

item_1.note: Case: Christopher Wilkerson, WC-MVA-[DOB-5]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson.

This narrative summarizes a series of email exchanges in late 2025 between The Whaley Law Firm, representing Christopher Wilkerson, and Harford Mutual Insurance Group, regarding the Christopher Wilkerson claim (238042CS). The emails, sent between October 27 and November 20, 2025, focus on settlement discussions and the exchange of medical records, with the usual attorney-client confidentiality notices included in each message. The May 2024 case involved a motor vehicle accident in the workers’ compensation context.

On October 27, 2025, Debbie Smith, Senior Claims Examiner at Harford Mutual Insurance Group, wrote to W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm. She noted that Mr. Wilkerson was last seen by a chiropractor in July 2025 and reminded that there had been a prior lump-sum settlement offer of $42,000. She also stated that she had settlement authority to resolve the claim for a lump-sum amount of $7,500 and asked Mr. Koon to indicate whether the claim could be resolved. The message included Debbie Smith’s contact information and the Harford Mutual disclaimer, and was cc’d to Christopher Wilkerson’s Filevine project email address.

On October 29, 2025, at 2:02 PM, Bryce Koon replied to Debbie Smith. He acknowledged that there were records from August and September that needed to be located and stated he would send them over ASAP. He also conveyed, on behalf of his client, that they must respectfully decline Harford Mutual’s offer. However, in an effort to reach an amicable settlement, he said they were prepared to decrease their demand to $38,000 for full and final closure of the claim. He signed the message as W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s Louisville address and contact information, and attached the customary confidentiality disclaimer.

Later that same day, at 4:46 PM, Debbie Smith replied that she would watch for the updated records. She commented that she felt the parties were very far apart and indicated she might consider scheduling Mr. Wilkerson for an independent medical examination (IME). The message included Debbie Smith’s contact details and the standard confidentiality disclaimer. The thread also shows that the correspondence continued to reference the same case and subject, Re: Christopher Wilkerson 238042CS.

On November 18, 2025, at 1:52 PM, Bryce Koon sent another message to Debbie Smith with the subject line Re: Christopher Wilkerson 238042CS. He stated that he was providing updated records he had received from Taylor County Chiropractic and invited Debbie to call him if she had questions or wished to discuss the claim. The message again included Bryce Koon’s signature block and the confidentiality disclaimer.

Finally, on November 20, 2025, at 5:01 PM, Bryce Koon wrote to Debbie Smith asking whether she had received the records he had sent. This message also carried the same confidentiality disclaimer and reflected the continuing exchange of records between the firm and the insurer as they pursued resolution of the claim.

Throughout these exchanges, the file references Mr. Wilkerson’s July 2025 chiropractic visit, August and September records that were being gathered, the parties’ ongoing settlement discussions (including a prior offer of $42,000 and an authority to settle for $7,500, with contemporaneous consideration of offers closer to $38,000 for full and final closure), and the potential for an IME as part of the resolution process. The communications were between W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm, Louisville, KY, and Debbie Smith, Senior Claims Examiner, Harford Mutual Insurance Group, with copy to Christopher Wilkerson’s Filevine project address.

item_2.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-8]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson.

In the email thread concerning Christopher Wilkerson’s workers’ compensation motor vehicle accident claim (238042CS), dated communications occurred between The Whaley Law Firm and Harford Mutual Insurance Group from late October to mid-November 2025. On October 27, 2025, Debbie Smith, Senior Claims Examiner for Harford Mutual, wrote that she had reviewed the file and noted that Mr. Wilkerson was last seen by the chiropractor in July 2025. She acknowledged the prior lump-sum settlement offer of $42,000 and stated that she had settlement authority to resolve the claim for a lump-sum amount of $7,500. She asked to know whether the claim could be resolved on that basis.

On October 29, 2025 at 2:02 PM, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, replied to Ms. Smith. He thanked her for the update and indicated that there were records from August and September floating around that he would send over as soon as possible. He then stated that, in the meantime, Harford Mutual’s offer would be respectfully declined. Nevertheless, in an effort to reach an amicable settlement, his office was prepared to decrease their demand to $38,000 for full and final closure of the claim.

Later on October 29, 2025 at 4:46 PM, Debbie Smith responded, thanking Mr. Koon and saying she would watch for the updated records. She commented that she felt the parties were very far apart and indicated she may consider scheduling the claimant for an independent medical examination (IME).

Finally, on November 18, 2025, at 01:52:39 GMT-05:00, Bryce Koon again addressed Debbie Smith. He forwarded updated records he had received from Taylor County Chiropractic and invited any questions or discussion about the claim, offering to be reached at the number listed below in his signature.

Throughout this correspondence, the parties referenced ongoing settlement discussions and the potential for updating medical records (specifically from August and September) as the negotiations proceeded. Each electronic message included The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information and a standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer noting that the message is intended only for the named recipient and should not be shared or used if received in error.

item_20.note: Case Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-959] involves client Christopher Wilkerson. Aaron Whaley has taken over the case, focusing on obtaining a doctor's report to aid in negotiations with the insurance company and on providing regular updates to Christopher moving forward.

Since assuming responsibility after the previous contact left the office, a demand was sent to the insurance company, which responded with zero based on the doctor's report. Aaron left a voicemail with the adjuster requesting the doctor's report to facilitate negotiations. Christopher expressed concern about the lack of updates and requested at least one to two updates per month, even if there is no progress. Aaron acknowledged the need for better communication and assured Christopher that he would keep him updated. item_46.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-182]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson. This note is a compilation of email communications between counsel, claims personnel, and related parties concerning the motor vehicle accident/workers’ compensation matter for Christopher Wilkerson (AFC 230577703). The messages include the settlement discussions and updates on Mr. Wilkerson’s employment status, as well as follow-up inquiries about the independent medical examination (IME) and the review of the claim.

On March 19, 2025, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent a confidential settlement demand to Debbie Smith on behalf of Mr. Wilkerson. The demand totaled $42,703.85 and was itemized as follows: 1) PPD (permanent partial disability) benefits in accordance with statutory calculations, based on an Average Weekly Wage (AWW) of $1,051.35 (as previously provided) and an 8% functional impairment rating per Dr. Jessica Leonard, Mr. Wilkerson’s treating physician, yielding a lump-sum PPD claim value of $17,703.35, with a printout of this calculation attached; 2) future medical expenses for physical therapy and pain management as indicated by Dr. Leonard’s report, estimated at approximately $15,000.00 (conservatively projected at $1,000.00 annually for the next 15 years); and 3) $10,000.00 for all additional waivers related to Mr. Wilkerson’s claim, including the right to reopen. The message closed with thanks for consideration and a note that the settlement demand was being submitted for the other side’s review.

On April 3, 2025 at 10:48 AM, Bryce Koon followed up with Debbie Smith, writing: Good morning Debbie, just wanted to follow up on this one again. Any update appreciated. He included the standard confidentiality language within his message.

On April 9, 2025 at 4:10 PM, Bryce Koon again wrote to Debbie Smith: Good afternoon Debbie, circling around on this one again. The message contained the same confidentiality language as prior messages.

On April 10, 2025 at 12:09 PM, Debbie Smith replied to Bryce. She stated that she had reviewed the IME report, sent the report out for a separate review, and expressed that she did not necessarily agree with the IME report. She anticipated completing her own review by the end of the following week and asked Bryce to confirm whether Mr. Wilkerson is currently working, and if so, where.

On April 29, 2025 at 2:58 PM, Bryce Koon responded to Debbie Smith with a direct confirmation: Yes. Mr. Wilkerson is presently employed with H&O Transport, Inc., located at 350 Industrial Drive, Campbellsville, KY 42718. He included the Whaley Law Firm contact information and maintained the standard confidentiality language found in the firm’s emails.

item_83.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-330]
Client: Christopher Wilkerson

RE: Christopher Wilkerson 238042

In a chain of communications regarding Mr. Christopher Wilkerson’s workers’ compensation claim (238042), Debbie Smith, Senior Claims Examiner for Clearpath Specialty Insurance, sent a message on January 20, 2025, to Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm, with Bryce Koon copied. Debbie reported that she had sent out several wage requests and had been able to call the employer’s office. She advised that she would email the wage request to the employer and asked that it be completed. Debbie noted that the employer indicated she had sent Mr. Wilkerson his 1099 form, which showed he was paid $7,597.11 for 2024. Debbie stated that once she received the wages, she would email a copy to the recipients. She signed the message and included a standard notice about faxing claim documents to [PHONE-331] and referencing the claim number. Her contact details were provided, including direct and main line numbers, and the message carried the confidentiality disclaimer typical of such communications.

Sarena Tuttle, in response later that same day, acknowledged the note and addressed the wage documentation issue. In her reply dated January 20, 2025 at 1:42 PM, she referenced the holiday season and circled back to the matter of Mr. Wilkerson’s AWW (Average Weekly Wages) documents from his employer. Sarena explained that the FROI (First Report of Injury) shows $10.00 per hour for 40 hours per week, which is not typical for a CDL driver pay type. She remarked that CDL drivers are usually paid more than $10.00 per hour and often have a per-mile or other additional rate on top of their hourly pay. She requested that Nathan Bennett Trucking’s payroll records be forwarded as soon as possible. Sarena provided her contact details and noted the newly updated email address for her correspondence.

Earlier in the chronology, Debbie Smith had written to Sarena on Saturday, November 9, 2024, to confirm that she was sending a request to the employer for a copy of Mr. Wilkerson’s wages. Debbie explained that, since this claim was medical-only, she had not requested wages initially. She stated that she had Mr. Wilkerson’s wages on the FROI as $10.00 per hour times 40 hours, equating to $400.00, and she would follow up with the employer for a response. Debbie offered to assist further if needed and again included the fax instruction and her signature block with confidential-disclaimer language.

Also in the earlier communications, there is a thread on October 10, 2024. At 10:07 AM, Sarena Tuttle forwarded a message to an external address, clarifying that while she understood the employer’s position on TTD (Temporary Total Disability) benefits, they were requesting documents related to the calculations of Mr. Wilkerson’s Average Weekly Wages. She stated that they were not currently asking the employer to initiate TTD, a matter to be addressed with Mrs. Smith. Regardless of the TTD status, she asserted that they were entitled to a copy of the documents obtained to calculate such benefits and that this request had been outstanding since the initiation of the claim.

Earlier on October 10, 2024, Kristi Woods (Claims Examiner for Clearpath Specialty Insurance) replied at 10:02 AM. In her message, she referred to Debbie’s file notes from August 13, 2024, noting that Debbie had approved physical therapy (PT X12) and was waiting on Mr. Wilkerson’s medical records to review any mention of TTD or medical status. Kristi indicated that once those records were received, they would have a better idea of how to move forward.

Throughout these exchanges, the parties repeatedly emphasized the confidentiality and privacy of the communications, attached files, and the fact that review of wages and calculations of Average Weekly Wages would inform the determination of benefits. The dialogue reflects efforts to obtain employer wage records (including 1099 forms and payroll data) to reconcile the FROI wage figures ($400 per week based on $10/hour for 40 hours) with any other reported compensation (notably the $7,597.11 shown on the 1099 for 2024) for Mr. Wilkerson’s claim. item_86.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-693]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson. This narrative covers the communications in late 2024 and early 2025 related to Mr. Wilkerson’s workers’ compensation claim (case number 238042) and the request for documents used to calculate his Average Weekly Wages (AWW).

On October 10, 2024, a thread began with Sarena Tuttle forwarding a message regarding Mr. Wilkerson’s claim to Kristi Woods (and cc’ing Bryce Koon). In the forwarded message, Sarena noted that their treatment update and a request for any and all documents related to Mr. Wilkerson’s average weekly wages were being supplied. She explained that they understood Mrs. Smith would be out of the office for the remainder of the week but emphasized the desire to obtain these documents as soon as possible. She also asked Kristi Woods to inform Mrs. Smith that her auto-reply email address was incorrect. The forwarding included Sarena’s standard contact details and signature.

Earlier that same day, at 9:39 AM, Sarena had sent the same forward to Kristi Woods with a public-facing disclaimer indicating the external origin of the email. The content of the forwarding stated that the Whaley Law Firm was providing the treatment update and reiterating the request for any and all documents related to Mr. Wilkerson’s average weekly wages and noted the willingness to proceed even though Mrs. Smith would be unavailable for the week. It also included Sarena’s confidentiality notice and her contact information.

Kristi Woods replied to Sarena on October 10, 2024 at 10:02 AM. In her response, she indicated she had reviewed the prior file notes from Debbie regarding Mr. Wilkerson’s claim, dated August 13, 2024. Kristi stated that Debbie had approved PT X12 and that she was waiting on Mr. Wilkerson’s medical records to review any mention of temporary total disability (TTD) or medical status. Kristi added that once the medical records were received, the team would have a clearer idea of how to move forward. The reply also contained the standard note advising recipients on faxing claim documents and included confidentiality language typical of the insurer’s communications.

At 10:07 AM on October 10, 2024, Sarena Tuttle responded. She opened with gratitude for Kristi Woods’s quick response that morning and then reiterated the Whaley Law Firm’s position. Specifically, she acknowledged the insurer’s stance on TTD benefits but emphasized that the documents related to the calculations of Mr. Wilkerson’s Average Weekly Wages were being requested. She clarified that they were not asking the insurer to initiate TTD at this time; that would be addressed with Mrs. Smith. Regardless of the TTD status, she maintained that the Whaley Law Firm was entitled to a copy of the documents used to calculate such benefits, a request that had been outstanding since the initiation of the claim. Sarena closed with her standard sign-off and contact information.

On November 9, 2024, Debbie Smith, Sr. Claims Examiner for ClearPath Specialty Insurance, replied to Sarena. Debbie confirmed that she was sending a request to Mr. Wilkerson’s employer for a copy of his wages. She explained that, because this was a medical-only claim, she had not previously requested wages. Debbie noted that the wages listed on the FROI were $10.00 per hour for 40 hours per week, equating to $400.00, and she said she would follow up with the employer for a response. She invited Sarena to let her know if anything else was needed. Debbie attached her contact details, including direct line [PHONE-340] and main line [PHONE-691], and included her email signature. The message also contained the standard confidentiality notice and the insurer’s social media icons, along with a customary warning about making fraudulent claims and the confidentiality restrictions for recipients.

Several related communications from 2024 also appear in the record. A prior message from Kristi Woods, dated October 10, 2024 at 10:02 AM, referenced Debbie’s file notes and ongoing work on PT X12, and again noted the need to obtain medical records to assess TTD and overall medical status before moving forward. The record also shows Debbie’s earlier note that the wage calculation on the FROI had already been captured as $10.00 per hour for 40 hours, totaling $400, and that additional wage records would be pursued if needed.

Finally, the document includes the initial email from January 20, 2025, in which Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm wrote to Debbie Smith and cc’d Bryce Koon. In this message, Sarena referenced Mr. Wilkerson’s AWW documents from his employer and reiterated that the wage structure on the FROI did not reflect typical CDL driver pay. She noted that CDL drivers are usually paid more than $10.00 per hour and often receive some form of per-mile pay on top of their hourly rate. Therefore, she requested that Nathan Bennett Trucking’s payroll records be forwarded as soon as possible. Sarena signaled that the new email address should be used for future correspondence and provided her direct line [PHONE-690] and office line [PHONE-343] ext 104, along with her email address.

In sum, the communications trace a concerted effort from The Whaley Law Firm (Sarena Tuttle) to obtain employer wage records and the calculations used to determine Mr. Wilkerson’s Average Weekly Wages, in the context of a medical-only workers’ compensation claim arising from a motor vehicle accident (case MVA-[DOB-688]) involving Christopher Wilkerson (claim number 238042). The involved insurer representatives ( Debbie Smith and Kristi Woods) discussed the status of medical records, PT authorization, and the potential impact of TTD, while repeatedly reaffirming the need for the employer’s wage data and payroll records from Nathan Bennett Trucking.

item_99.note: Case: Christopher Wilkerson WC-MVA-[DOB-645]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson. The matter at hand concerns claim number 238042, with The Whaley Law Firm representing the claimant and ClearPath Specialty Insurance issuing the handling notes.

The Whaley Law Firm’s contact details were included, and the message again noted Mrs. Smith’s anticipated absence.

Debbie planned to follow up with the employer for a response and asked to be notified if any additional information was needed. Debbie provided the contact details for her office (Direct: [PHONE-388]; Main: [PHONE-389]) and reminded recipients of the fax reference process for claim documents (to fax to [PHONE-390] and reference the claim number). The November 9, 2024 message also included Debbie’s signature block and the confidentiality notice typical of these communications.

Throughout these interactions, the communications referenced the confidential and restricted nature of the information, the need to limit distribution to the addressee(s) named, and the penalties for presenting fraudulent information. It is also noted in the communications that The Whaley Law Firm’s staff included Sarena M. Tuttle (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; D: [PHONE-641]; O: [PHONE-392] ext. 104; E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com; new email address indicated) and Kristi Woods (Claims Examiner at ClearPath Specialty Insurance; Direct: [PHONE-393]; Main: [PHONE-638]). ClearPath Specialty Insurance’s notice sections reiterate that misrepresentation or fraudulent claims are crimes and that confidential communications must be treated accordingly.

item_103.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-415]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson.

In October 2024, the Whaley Law Firm sent a forward of communications regarding Mr. Wilkerson’s workers’ compensation matter, titled “Fwd: Christopher Wilkerson 238042.” The message, dated October 8, 2024, was from Sarena Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, to Mrs. Woods, with CCs to Bryce Koon and others. It requested treatment updates and “any and all documents related to Mr. Wilkerson’s average weekly wages,” noting that Mrs. Smith would be out of the office for the remainder of the week but that the documents were needed as soon as possible. The email signature identified Sarena M. Tuttle and included her contact information and a notification to note the new email address.

The forwarded thread contains a subsequent message from Sarena Tuttle, dated October 8, 2024 at 1:56 PM, addressed to Debbie Smith with CCs to Greg Whaley and Bryce Koon. In this message, they reported having spoken with Mr. Wilkerson and his treating physician. They updated that Mr. Wilkerson had been given the opportunity to see how his injuries would respond under normal working conditions, but his condition has not improved and he has returned to treatment. The team stated they were working with his provider to ensure he receives the necessary treatment to reduce pain while working and to move toward a maximum medical improvement (MMI) standpoint. They also requested a copy of any and all documents used to calculate his average weekly wages for the incident.

This October thread followed earlier communications from August 2024. On August 27, 2024 at 1:29 PM, Sarena Tuttle wrote to Debbie Smith (with CCs to Greg Whaley and Bryce Koon) that Mr. Wilkerson’s last day of work was August 2, 2024. She attached certified medical records from Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation, which indicated that Mr. Wilkerson’s seated occupation was causing limited or delayed progress/response to care. The message stated that Mr. Wilkerson had been terminated from employment due to missing too many days for treatment and that, at this time, he would like to receive temporary total disability (TTD) benefits to assist with treatment and recovery until he could return to full-time work. They asked Debbie Smith to update them on whether TTD initiation had begun and to contact them if anything else was needed to discuss the matter.

The August 27 message was preceded by an August 26, 2024 note in which Sarena Tuttle replied, “Good morning Debbie, That is awesome. Thank you so much,” expressing thanks.

Earlier, on August 23, 2024 at 5:16 PM, Debbie Smith replied that she had faxed approval for 12 therapy visits and requested updated notes for the off-work status so she could review the file for lost time. The reply included standard confidentiality and contact disclaimers and references to claiming documents going by fax to [PHONE-616] with the instruction to reference the claim number. Debbie Smith identified her role as Sr. Claims Examiner at Clearpath Specialty Insurance, with direct and main contact numbers provided.

Also on August 23, 2024 at 2:23 PM, Sarena Tuttle sent another message (labeled as external in the chain) to Debbie Smith, noting that Mr. Wilkerson had reached out again, indicating that his physical therapy had not yet been approved. They requested clarification on what was needed to get his PT approved and stated they were awaiting medical records for his TTD benefits at that time.

The chronology also includes an August 12, 2024 message from Sarena Tuttle at 1:38 PM to Debbie Smith. In this message, they reported receiving a call from Mr. Wilkerson stating that he had been terminated from his position due to his medical treatment and continued appointments. They again requested initiation of his TTD benefits and invited further discussion if there were questions or issues.

Additionally, on July 24, 2024, at 12:06 PM, Sarena Tuttle wrote to Debbie Smith (and CC’d Greg Whaley and Bryce Koon) reporting that Mr. Wilkerson was unhappy with the treatment at Grant Chiropractic. Dr. Grant had advised that because Mr. Wilkerson had exhausted his initial 20 visits, the claim had ended. Mr. Wilkerson had scheduled an appointment with Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation on Greenbriar Drive in Campbellsville, KY for July 29, 2024. The email included attachment of the updated Kentucky Division of Workers’ Compensation Form 113 for Taylor Co. Chiro and invited any questions.

In summary, between July and October 2024, Mr. Wilkerson’s case involved: termination from employment on account of medical treatment and attendance, initiation and pursuit of TTD benefits, scheduling and switching between chiropractors (Grant Chiropractic to Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation), approval and scheduling of therapy visits (12 therapy visits approved), ongoing requests for documentation to calculate average weekly wages, updates on treatment status and progress toward maximum medical improvement, and repeated requests for medical records to support disability and wage calculations. item_140.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-543]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson. This narrative covers the communications surrounding Christopher Wilkerson’s workers’ compensation matter (Christopher Wilkerson 238042) from spring through late summer 2024, including treatment updates, employment status, and requests for temporary total disability (TTD) benefits.

In the sequence of communications, Debbie Smith at ClearPath Specialty Insurance (now operating under Harford Mutual Insurance Group, with the newer hm1842.com domain) received an update from The Whaley Law Firm on April 5, 2024 noting the domain change and instructing others to update contact lists accordingly. Debbie’s message explained that all ClearPath emails had transitioned to the hm1842.com extension due to the merger with Harford Mutual; recipients were asked to update their contact lists to ensure efficient handling of email correspondence.

On July 24, 2024, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm informed Debbie that Mr. Wilkerson was not satisfied with treatment at Grant Chiropractic. Dr. Grant advised that because Mr. Wilkerson had exhausted his initial 20 visits, the claim had ended. Mr. Wilkerson had scheduled an appointment with Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation on Greenbriar Drive in Campbellsville, KY for July 29, 2024. Sarena noted that the updated Kentucky Department of Workers’ Claims Form 113 for Taylor Co. Chiro was attached to that communication.

By August 12, 2024, Sarena Tuttle reported that Mr. Wilkerson had called earlier that morning to say he had been terminated from his position due to his medical treatment and ongoing appointments. At that time, she reiterated the request for initiation of TTD Benefits and asked Debbie to contact their office if there were questions or issues with the request.

On August 23, 2024 at 2:23 PM, Sarena again wrote to Debbie (with Greg Whaley and Bryce Koon cc’d) that Mr. Wilkerson had contacted them again, this time indicating that his Physical Therapy had not yet been approved. She requested an update on what was needed to obtain PT approval and noted that they were awaiting medical records for his TTD benefits.

That same day, August 23, 2024, Debbie Smith replied at 5:16 PM, stating that she had faxed approval for 12 therapy visits. Debbie asked that The Whaley Law Firm provide updated notes for Mr. Wilkerson’s off-work status so she could review the file for lost time. Debbie’s signature identified her as Senior Claims Examiner for ClearPath Specialty Insurance, with Direct and Main phone numbers listed, and she included the standard confidentiality and external-email notices that accompany such communications. The message also contained the customary reminder to reference the claim number when faxing claim documents and to be aware of the newly updated hm1842.com email addresses.

Later on August 26, 2024 at 9:34 AM, Sarena Tuttle replied to Debbie with a brief, courteous note: “That is awesome. Thank you so much.” This acknowledged the earlier step of PT approval and related documentation.

The latest substantive update came on August 27, 2024. In that message, Sarena Tuttle advised Debbie that Mr. Wilkerson’s last day of work had been August 2, 2024. She attached certified medical records from Taylor Co. Chiro & Rehab, which stated that Mr. Wilkerson’s seated occupation was contributing to limited and delayed progress/response to care. The communication noted that Mr. Wilkerson had been terminated from employment due to missing too many days for treatment, and he was requesting TTD benefits to support his treatment and recovery until he could return to full-time work. Sarena requested an update on the initiation of his TTD benefits and invited Debbie to contact her directly to discuss any further needs.

Contact details for ongoing communications remained with Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222. Her direct line was [PHONE-544], and her office line was [PHONE-545] ext 104, with the email address Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (noting the new address). Debbie Smith’s role as Sr. Claims Examiner for ClearPath Specialty Insurance (now hm1842 domain) continued with Direct: [PHONE-546] and Main: [PHONE-547], and included similar confidentiality notices in correspondence.

In summary, the case details reflect Mr. Wilkerson’s termination from employment on August 2, 2024 due to attendance issues related to his medical treatment, the attachment of Taylor Co. chiropractic records indicating a seated occupation contributing to slow progress, and a request for TTD benefits to support treatment and recovery until he can return to full-time work. There were approvals for 12 therapy visits, requests for updated off-work notes to support lost-time review, and ongoing dialogue between The Whaley Law Firm and ClearPath/Harford Mutual representatives to address PT approval and TTD initiation.

item_150.note: Case: Christopher Wilkerson, WC-MVA-[DOB-568]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson. This matter concerns a workers’ compensation claim (Christopher Wilkerson, 238042) arising from a motor vehicle accident on February 15, 2024. The Whaley Law Firm represents Mr. Wilkerson, with Sarena M. Tuttle serving as the litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager. The correspondence in this file involves Debbie Smith, a Senior Claims Examiner for ClearPath Specialty Insurance, later operating under Harford Mutual Insurance Group after a merger, and members of the Whaley team including Greg Whaley and Bryce Koon. The case file contains multiple communications spanning April through August 2024.

On April 5, 2024, Debbie Smith advised that ClearPath had accepted the claim as compensable, but there were no medical records to verify any off-work status, and she indicated that those records had been requested. Later that same day, Sarena Tuttle responded with attachments: the executed Form 106 and Form 113. She noted that Mr. Wilkerson was still receiving treatment with Dr. Anthony Grant at Grant Chiropractic Center in Columbia, Kentucky, and that all medical records to date had been requested and were awaited; as soon as records began arriving, they would be forwarded.

The thread continued with additional updates over the ensuing months. On July 24, 2024, Sarena reported that Mr. Wilkerson was not happy with the treatment at Grant Chiropractic, and that Dr. Grant had advised that since Mr. Wilkerson had exhausted his initial 20 visit allowance, his claim had ended. Mr. Wilkerson subsequently scheduled an appointment with Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation on Greenbriar Drive in Campbellsville, Kentucky for July 29, 2024. An updated KY Division of Workers’ Compensation Form 113 for Taylor Co. Chiropractic was attached.

By August 12, 2024, Sarena informed Debbie that Mr. Wilkerson had called to report he had been terminated from his position due to his medical treatment and ongoing appointments, and that initiation of his Temporary Total Disability (TTD) benefits was requested.

On August 23, 2024, Debbie indicated that she had faxed approval for 12 therapy visits and requested updated notes on the off-work status so she could review the file for lost time. Later that day, at 2:23 PM, Sarena responded that Mr. Wilkerson had again contacted them, stating that his physical therapy had not yet been approved and asking what was needed to obtain PT approval; she also noted that they were awaiting medical records for TTD benefits.

That same day, Debbie reiterated the status of the PT approval by stating that 12 therapy visits had been approved by the insurer. The thread included standard reminders about confidentiality and the external origin of some emails, and also contained the insurer’s new contact information following the merger with Harford Mutual Insurance Group: Debbie’s message reminded that, due to the merger, all ClearPath email addresses had changed to the hm1842.com domain. In the Whaley firm signature blocks, Sarena noted the new email address and included her contact details: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; direct line [PHONE-569]; office line [PHONE-570] ext 104; email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, with a note to “PLEASE NOTE NEW EMAIL ADDRESS.”

On August 26, 2024, Sarena sent a brief closing note: “Good morning Debbie, That is awesome. Thank you so much.” Her message was followed by the standard firm signature block, including a reminder of her new email address.

Throughout these communications, the case remained identified as Christopher Wilkerson, 238042, with the overarching matter being a workers’ compensation claim associated with a motor vehicle incident dated February 15, 2024. The communications document ongoing efforts to obtain therapeutic approvals (initial therapy visits and later therapy approval), medical records to support off-work status and TTD benefits, changes in treating providers (Grant Chiropractic to Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation), and the associated administrative actions required by both the insurer and the law firm to move the claim forward.

item_153.note: The case Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-577] involves client Christopher Wilkerson. The communications center on April 2024, when Debbie Smith, Sr. Claims Examiner for ClearPath Specialty Insurance (later referred to after the merger as Harford Mutual Insurance Group, with email addresses transitioning to the hm1842.com domain), advised The Whaley Law Firm that ClearPath had accepted the claim as compensable but that there were no medical records yet to verify any off-work status. Debbie noted that she had requested medical records from Ephraim McDowell, Grant Chiropractic, and Adair Family Medical, and she needed a copy of the medical authorization and the KY Department of Workers’ Claims Form 113 to confirm the designated physician. She also asked that any medical records be forwarded for review and added that the employer did not have a copy of dash cam footage of the accident. She supplied her direct and main contact numbers and included confidential‑communication notices customary for the insurer.

Shortly after, on the same thread, Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager for The Whaley Law Firm, responded on April 5, 2024. She advised that she was attaching the executed Form 106 and Form 113, and she stated that Mr. Wilkerson was still currently treating with Dr. Anthony Grant at Grant Chiropractic Center in Columbia, Kentucky. She noted that they had requested all medical records to date and were awaiting receipt of those records, and that once they began receiving them, they would forward them to Debbie for review.

Also on April 5, 2024, Debbie’s message confirmed that ClearPath had accepted the claim as compensable but reiterated the lack of medical records to verify off-work status and the need for medical authorizations and Form 113. She indicated she had requested records from Ephraim McDowell, Grant Chiropractic, and Adair Family Medical, and she again asked for a copy of the medical authorization and Form 113 to confirm the designated physician, adding that if any medical records were available, they should be forwarded. Debbie also confirmed with The Whaley Law Firm that the employer did not possess dash cam footage of the accident. In the same thread, Debbie reminded that, due to the merger with Harford Mutual Insurance Group, all ClearPath email addresses had transitioned to the hm1842.com extension.

Earlier in the thread, on April 5, 2024 (with timestamps in the exchanged emails), Sarena had also sent a separate note to Debbie noting that Chris was still treating with Dr. Grant and that Form 106 and Form 113 had been attached. She stated that they had requested all medical records to date and would forward them as soon as they were received.

By July 24, 2024, the communications indicate a shift in Mr. Wilkerson’s treatment experience. In an email from Sarena, she reported that Mr. Wilkerson was not happy with the treatment at Grant Chiropractic, and Dr. Grant advised that since Mr. Wilkerson had exhausted his initial 20 visits, the claim had ended. Mr. Wilkerson had made an appointment with Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation on Greenbriar Drive in Campbellsville, Kentucky for July 29, 2024. The email also notes that the updated Kentucky DWC Form 113 for Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation was attached, and Sarena invited Debbie to contact them directly if there were questions for further discussion.

On August 12, 2024 at 1:38 PM, Sarena notified Debbie that Mr. Wilkerson had been terminated from his job due to his medical treatment and ongoing appointments, and she requested initiation of his Temporary Total Disability (TTD) benefits, asking The Whaley Law Firm to contact their office if there were any questions or issues regarding the request.

By August 23, 2024, the thread shows ongoing concerns about therapy approval. At 2:23 PM, Sarena wrote that Mr. Wilkerson had contacted them again, advising that his physical therapy had not yet been approved. She asked Debbie to update them on what was required to obtain approval for his physical therapy and indicated that they were awaiting medical records for his TTD benefits.

That same day, at 9:16 PM, Debbie replied to Sarena. She stated that she had faxed approval for 12 therapy visits and requested updated notes for off-work status so she could review the file for lost time. Debbie closed with thanks and included the standard confidentiality and privacy disclaimers associated with her communications.

Throughout these exchanges, the correspondence also carried standard headers and notices. The messages emphasized confidentiality and the restricted distribution of attachments, reminded recipients that the communications were intended solely for the named addressees, and advised that the merger had caused the @clearpathmutual.com addresses to become @hm1842.com addresses. The Whaley Law Firm’s contact details and Dr. Grant’s and Taylor Co. Chiropractic’s involvement were repeatedly referenced, along with status updates on medical records, Form 106, Form 113, and the designation of the physician, as well as the ongoing issue of off-work status and lost-time review.

item_168.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-633]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson.

This narrative covers the communications regarding Christopher Wilkerson’s workers’ compensation claim (Claim No. 238042) as handled by The Whaley Law Firm and the claims administrator, Harford Mutual Insurance Group (domain hm1842.com), from March 2024 through August 2024. The Whaley Law Firm represented Mr. Wilkerson in the matter, with Sarena M. Tuttle serving as Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager. The firm’s contact details were: 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; direct line [PHONE-634]; office line [PHONE-635] ext 104; email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (noting the address change to the new domain).

On March 20, 2024, Sarena Tuttle sent a message to Debbie Smith indicating that, to date, they had not received a compensability decision from Harford Mutual nor an acknowledgement of their prior email requesting confirmation from Mr. Wilkerson about whether there was dash cam footage of the incident. She attached the Employee’s Statement Questionnaire and invited Debbie to contact them directly if anything else was needed.

In early April 2024, the communications continued as follows: Debbie Smith responded on April 5, 2024, confirming that ClearPath had accepted the claim as compensable, but noting that there were no medical records to verify any off-work status. Debbie stated that medical records were being requested from Ephraim McDowell, Grant Chiropractic, and Adair Family Medical, and that a copy of the medical authorization and KY DWC Form 113 was needed to confirm the designated physician. She asked that any medical records be forwarded for review and noted that the employer did not have dash cam footage of the accident. In the same thread, Debbie’s message included a reminder about the merger that had changed all @clearpathmutual.com addresses to the @hm1842.com extension and urged updating contact lists accordingly. Earlier in the day, Sarena had informed Debbie that Form 106 and Form 113 had been executed, and that Chris was still receiving treatment with Dr. Anthony Grant at Grant Chiropractic Center in Columbia, KY. They were awaiting receipt of medical records to date and planned to forward them as soon as they were received.

Throughout April 2024, the exchange continued with regard to medical records and treating providers. Debe’s notes reiterate the need for medical records and the Form 113 to confirm the designated physician; the team also confirmed that they were seeking medical records from Ephraim McDowell, Grant Chiropractic, and Adair Family Medical, and they requested any available records be forwarded for review. There is also mention of continued discussion about whether dash cam footage existed, with the employer specifically stating they did not have any dash cam footage of the accident.

On July 24, 2024, Sarena Tuttle provided an updated status. She advised Debbie that Mr. Wilkerson was unhappy with the treatment at Grant Chiropractic and that Dr. Grant had told him that after exhausting his initial 20 visits, his claim had ended. Mr. Wilkerson had scheduled an appointment with Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation on Greenbriar Drive in Campbellsville, KY for July 29, 2024. The message noted the attachment of an updated KY DWC Form 113 for Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation and invited any questions or further discussion.

Finally, on August 12, 2024, Sarena Tuttle sent another update. She reported that Mr. Wilkerson had called that morning to say he had been terminated from his job due to his medical treatment and ongoing appointments. The Whaley Law Firm requested the initiation of his temporary total disability (TTD) benefits and asked Debbie Smith to contact them if there were any questions or issues with the request.

In sum, the record reflects a series of communications between The Whaley Law Firm and Harford Mutual (HM) regarding Christopher Wilkerson’s workers’ compensation claim, covering March through August 2024. Key elements include ongoing medical treatment with Grant Chiropractic (and later Taylor Co. Chiropractic & Rehabilitation), a claim acceptance as compensable, the need for medical records and Form 113 to designate the physician, dash cam footage status, and finally the request to commence TTD benefits after Mr. Wilkerson reported termination from employment due to medical treatment. Attachments mentioned in the exchanges include the executed Form 106 and Form 113 (as of April 5, 2024) and an updated KY DWC Form 113 for Taylor Co. Chiropractic (as of July 24, 2024).

item_200.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-726]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson.

Initial client contact on May 9, 2024, by Sarena regarding Christopher Wilkerson’s motor vehicle accident on February 15, 2024 and a possible wrongful termination claim. The client reported that he was fired after just one accident, while another employee, Jonathan Vaughn, remains employed after three accidents. He also stated that Nathan Bennett is not properly registered with Safety Clearinghouse and does not drug test their employees prior to putting them behind the wheel. I advised that I would update AW/BK on this for consideration of a wrongful termination (WFT) suit, and I explained that Kentucky is an at-will state, which allows employers to terminate with little or no reason, making WFT claims difficult. The client expressed understanding.

We also spoke about treatment status. Dr. Grant is thinking he may refer the client to another provider, but did not elaborate. The client states he is still experiencing pain in his hip and ribs nearly 90 days post-accident. We discussed the possibility of a tear or a pinched nerve in the hip and advised the client to discuss this with Dr. Grant further and to see if additional imaging should be requested. The client expressed understanding and will discuss at his next appointment on May 11.

Additionally, we discussed how workers’ compensation claims are valued and that it is impossible to begin discussing dollar amounts due to impairment weight in the formula. The client expressed understanding and appreciated the time taken to explain the process. He will call us with an update after his appointment on Saturday, May 11.

item_207.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-751]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson. This matter concerns Christopher Wilkerson, with the file referenced as Christopher Wilkerson 238042.

On April 5, 2024, Debbie Smith, Senior Claims Examiner for Harford Mutual Insurance Group, sent a message to Sarena Tuttle confirming that ClearPath has accepted the claim as compensable. Debbie noted, however, that she had no medical records to verify any off-work status and that she had requested medical records from Ephraim McDowell, Grant Chiropractic, and Adair Family Medical. Debbie signed as Sr. Claims Examiner and provided her contact information, and the message carried the usual confidentiality and misaddress disclaimers typical of such communications.

In the prior correspondence, on March 6, 2024, Debbie Smith acknowledged Mr. Whaley’s representation of Mr. Wilkerson, stating that once the reviewing of the information is completed and any questions arise, she would be in touch. The next day, March 7, 2024, Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm replied, noting that they had not yet received a compensability decision from Debbie’s office, nor had they received acknowledgment of the firm’s prior request to confirm whether the incident involved any dash cam footage. Sarena informed Debbie that the Employee's Statement Questionnaire had been attached as requested and invited further discussion if more information was needed. She included her contact details and reminded that her email address was the newly updated one.

Earlier, on March 7, 2024, Sarena’s message also conveyed that, at that time, the driver of the “Black KIA” had not been identified, and requested the insured to advise whether the vehicle driven by Mr. Wilkerson was equipped with a dash cam or any recording device. If such a device existed, they asked that recordings—whether video, audio, written, verbal, or otherwise—be preserved and forwarded to their office for review and to aid in the investigation of the driver of the Black KIA.

Then, on March 6, 2024, Debbie Smith had written to acknowledge Mr. Whaley’s representation, indicating that upon review of the information and any questions arising, she would reach out. The March 20, 2024 communication from Sarena reiterates that no compensability decision had yet been provided and notes again the need for confirmation regarding dash cam footage; it also confirms that the Employee's Statement Questionnaire was sent as requested and reiterates that the firm is available to discuss the matter further.

Additionally, the thread contains standard email footers reflecting a recent merger and the associated changes of domain, and includes confidentiality notices typical of such communications. It also contains a cautionary note within one message about an external email and an automatic notice indicating the email’s origin outside the organization.

In summary, after an initial representation acknowledgment, the parties discussed dash cam footage and the identity of the vehicle driver, with the Whaley firm supplying the Employee's Statement Questionnaire. By early April 2024, ClearPath/ClearPath-mutual records indicated the claim was accepted as compensable, but medical records to establish off-work status were still outstanding, with Debbie Smith requesting medical records from specified providers and copies of the medical authorization and Form 113 to confirm the designated physician, while also confirming the absence of dash cam footage in the employer’s records.

item_208.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-753]
Client: Christopher Wilkerson

In early 2024, the Christopher Wilkerson case (WC MVA, file 238042) unfolded as a communications exchange between The Whaley Law Firm and Harford Mutual Insurance Group (formerly ClearPath Mutual). The sequence begins with Debbie Smith, a Senior Claims Examiner for Harford Mutual, acknowledging the Whaley Law Firm’s representation of Mr. Wilkerson. In an email dated March 6, 2024, she stated, “Please find my acknowledgement letter of Mr. Whaley’s representation of Mr. Wilkerson,” and noted the merger with Harford Mutual that had changed all @clearpathmutual.com addresses to @hm1842.com, advising the recipient to update their contact list. Debbie signed with her contact information and included confidentiality language typical of the communications.

The following day, March 7, 2024, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm replied to Debbie’s acknowledgement. She expressed appreciation for the acknowledgement and indicated that once the Whaley firm received the requested questionnaire, they would forward all documents to Harford Mutual. She also noted that the driver of the Black KIA involved in the incident had not yet been identified and asked Debbie’s insured to confirm whether the vehicle operated by Mr. Wilkerson was equipped with a dash cam or any recording device. If such a device existed, the Whaley firm requested preservation of all recordings and that copies be forwarded to their office for review and to aid in identifying the driver of the Black KIA. The message included Sarena’s contact details and reminded recipients of the new email address.

On March 20, 2024, the thread continued with another communication from The Whaley Law Firm. Sarena Tuttle wrote that, to date, they had not received a compensability decision from Harford Mutual nor an acknowledgment of their earlier request regarding dash cam footage. She attached the Employee’s Statement Questionnaire as requested and invited Debbie to contact them if anything else was needed. The email reiterated the ongoing contact information for Sarena and again included the new email address.

Further correspondence followed on March 7 and March 20 that focused on the status of the investigation and the documentation needed. By March 20, the Whaley firm had provided the Employee’s Statement Questionnaire, and they reminded Harford Mutual to communicate any additional requirements so that the matter could proceed.

On April 5, 2024, the timeline shows two significant contributions from Debbie Smith and The Whaley Law Firm. At 9:29 AM, Debbie wrote to Sarena confirming that ClearPath had accepted the claim as compensable. She noted that she did not yet have medical records to verify any off-work status and that she had requested medical records from Ephraim McDowell, Grant Chiropractic, and Adair Family Medical. Debbie also requested a copy of the medical authorization and Form 113 to confirm the designated physician and asked that any available medical records be forwarded for her review. She added that she had confirmed with the employer that they did not possess any dash cam footage of the accident. Debbie closed with thanks.

Shortly thereafter, at 9:46 AM, Sarena responded with a message confirming that the claim remained compensable. She attached the executed Form 106 and Form 113 and provided details about Mr. Wilkerson’s current treatment: he was still seeing Dr. Anthony Grant at Grant Chiropractic Center in Columbia, Kentucky. She stated that all available medical records had been requested and were being sought, and she would forward them to Debbie as they were received. Sarena noted that the firm had already requested all medical records to date and would forward them when obtained. She also reaffirmed the new Harford Mutual contact information and included the standard confidentiality and external-origin notices found in the correspondence.

Throughout the April 5 exchanges, the notices regarding the merger remained prominent, reminding recipients that all @clearpathmutual.com addresses had been migrated to the @hm1842.com extension, and encouraging updating of contact lists for efficient handling. The emails also contained the customary confidential-use notices and warnings about handling confidential information and about false or fraudulent claims.

Key facts preserved from the correspondence:
- Case: Christopher Wilkerson, WC MVA case, file reference Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-754]; Client: Christopher Wilkerson; Claim number or internal reference 238042.
- Parties involved: The Whaley Law Firm (Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager) and Harford Mutual Insurance Group (formerly ClearPath Mutual) via Debbie Smith (Senior Claims Examiner) and other Harford Mutual communications staff.
- Timeline of material communications: 
  - March 6, 2024: Debbie Smith acknowledges Whaley’s representation (merger-related email domain change noted).
  - March 7, 2024: Sarena Tuttle requests the dash cam/recording-device information and preservation of any recordings; driver of Black KIA not identified.
  - March 20, 2024: Sarena notes no compensability decision received and attaches Employee’s Statement Questionnaire; reiterates request regarding dash cam footage.
  - March 20, 2024: (Earlier in the thread) The Whaley firm sent the Employee’s Statement Questionnaire; continued to pursue information.
  - April 5, 2024: Debbie confirms that ClearPath has accepted the claim as compensable; medical-records status pending; requests medical records from Ephraim McDowell, Grant Chiropractic, and Adair Family Medical; requests medical authorization and Form 113 to confirm the designated physician; confirms no dash cam footage is in the employer’s possession.
  - April 5, 2024: Sarena confirms compensable status and forwards Form 106 and Form 113 as executed; notes ongoing treatment with Dr. Anthony Grant at Grant Chiropractic Center; states that medical records have been requested and will be forwarded as they are received.

item_230.note: Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-818]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson. This concerns Claim 04943051 for Christopher Wilkerson.

On March 14, 2024, the Whaley Law Firm’s Sarena M. Tuttle sent an email to Megan Bates of Kentucky Farm Bureau Insurance regarding Mr. Wilkerson’s claim. She attached Mr. Wilkerson’s executed PIP Application and explained that the recorded statement needed to be rescheduled, asking Bates what date and time would work. Sarena’s contact details at the time were The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with D: [PHONE-819] and O: [PHONE-820] ext 104, and her email listed as Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (noting the new email address in the signature).

Megan Bates, a Claim Adjuster II for Kentucky Farm Bureau Insurance at the Campbellsville Regional Office, replied on March 18, 2024 at 11:04 AM with, “Hey Sarena, Would a time on Wednesday work for you all?” Bates’ signature also included her office details: 110 Nancy Cox Drive, Campbellsville, KY 42718; mailing address PO Box 20400, Louisville, KY 40250-9802; Office: [PHONE-821]; Cell: [PHONE-822]; Fax: [PHONE-823]; kyfb.com | Member login.

In response, on March 18, 2024 at 11:19 AM, Sarena stated, “Good morning Megan, Let me check in with Mr. Wilkerson and see what time works best for him. As a truck driver, we obviously do not want to schedule this while he is driving.” Her signature again listed her role as Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, with the same contact details, and again noting her email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (PLEASE NOTE NEW EMAIL ADDRESS).

Later that same day, at 11:29 AM, Sarena informed Bates, “Mr. Wilkerson is available at 10am.” Bates then replied, “That works for me!” at 20:03:49 +0000, confirming the time.

Summary of participants and contact details:
- Case: Christopher-Wilkerson-WC-MVA-[DOB-824]. Client: Christopher Wilkerson.
- The Whaley Law Firm contact: Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; D: [PHONE-825]; O: [PHONE-826] ext 104; E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (NEW EMAIL ADDRESS noted in signature).

Bates inquired whether a time on Wednesday would work for all parties and provided her contact information: 110 Nancy Cox Drive, Campbellsville, KY 42718; PO Box 20400, Louisville, KY 40250-9802; Office phone [PHONE-838]; Cell [PHONE-839]; Fax [PHONE-840]; kyfb.com.

Finally, at 11:28 AM on March 18, 2024, Sarena informed Megan that Mr. Wilkerson is available at 10:00 AM. In her signature, Sarena provided The Whaley Law Firm’s contact details: 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; direct line [PHONE-841]; office line [PHONE-842] ext 104; email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, with a note to please use the new email address. On March 12, 2024, at 10:14:26 AM Pacific Time, DocuSign emailed Aaron Whaley ([EMAIL-891]) from [EMAIL-892] to note that all signers had completed the signing process and that The Whaley Law Firm had requested Aaron Whaley’s signature. The message directed him to review the document the recipients have signed and to review the following payment(s) via the link: https://na4.docusign.net/Member/EmailStart.aspx?m=321891ae-c9ab-45d1-8eec-08d8fb4fede0. If the link did not work, he was advised to highlight and copy the entire line and paste it into his browser to get started.

The email stated that it was sent to him by Aaron Whaley, who is using the DocuSign Electronic Signature Service. It included notices that he would not be contacted by this sender if he preferred not to receive emails, and it warned, “Do Not Share This Email,” noting that the email contains a secure DocuSign link and that the link or access code should not be shared with others.
